## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration (dv_dt) in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force and/or damping depend nonlinearly on position x and velocity v, possibly with external time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced cubic oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum with drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity / asymmetric potential)
- General polynomial restoring + damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (combined nonlinearities)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of the potential well, indicating symmetric oscillations around equilibrium
- Even-power terms in position (x**2) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells (Helmholtz-type)
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Products of position powers with velocity (x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate periodic potential landscapes or geometric nonlinearity (pendulum)
- Sinusoidal functions of time cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms with opposite sign to linear term (c0*x - c1*x**3 with c0,c1>0) indicate a hardening or softening spring depending on sign convention
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests autonomous/conservative or dissipative system without external forcing

GT Equivalence Verification (PO21)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can be made equivalent to the GT: `0.767518*sin(t) - 0.263896*v*sin(x)`.

Note that `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2) = cos(π/2 + t)` and `-sin(x)` is not easily expressible using the terms available in most candidates.

The GT has two terms:
1. `F0*sin(t)` — a function of t only
2. `-beta*v*sin(x)` — a product of v and a function of x

The key challenge is the `v*sin(x)` term. Most candidates don't have `sin(x)` directly but have terms like `v*sin(c*t + c)`, `v*cos(c*t + c)`, `v*x`, `v/x^5`, etc.

Let me check which candidates could produce a `v*sin(x)` term (a function of x times v, independent of t):

**Candidates with `v*x*cos(c*t + c)` terms** (1,2,3,4,6,9,13,22,35,43): Setting the t-frequency to 0 gives `v*x*cos(c)` = `c*v*x`, which is linear in x, not sin(x). These can't produce `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidates with `v*sin(c*t + c)` terms**: If the frequency of t is set to 0, this becomes `v*sin(c)` = constant*v. This can't produce `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidates with `v*cos(c*t + c)` terms**: Similarly becomes constant*v.

**Candidate 47**: `c0*cos(c1+t) + c2*v*x + c3*v*sin(c4*t+c5) + c6*exp(c7*v)`. Has `v*x` (linear), not `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidate 32**: `c0*t + c1*x + c2*v*cos(c3*t+c4) + c5*sin(c6+c7*x+c8*v) + x^c9`. The sin term is `sin(c6+c7*x+c8*v)`, but this isn't multiplied by v. We need `v*sin(x)`, not `sin(x)`.

**Candidate 12**: `c0*t + c1*x + c2*sin(c3*x+c4) + c5*cos(c6+t) + c7*v*sin(c8*t+c9)`. Has `sin(c3*x+c4)` but not multiplied by v. Can't produce `v*sin(x)`.

**Candidate 38**: Has `c7*v*x^c8` — setting c8 to specific values gives power-law terms, not sin(x).

**Candidate 42**: `c0*t + c1*x + c2*x^c3 + c4*v*cos(c5*t+c6) + c7*v*sin(c8*t+c9)`. The v terms depend on t, not x.

None of the candidates have a term of the form `v*f(x)` where f(x) can be sin(x). The `v*sin(...)` terms always have t-dependence in the argument, and setting the t-coefficient to 0 just gives a constant times v. The `v*x*cos(...)` terms give at best `v*x` (linear). The `sin(c*x+c)` terms in candidate 12 aren't multiplied by v.

The term `-beta*v*sin(x)` requires a product of v with a nonlinear function of x (specifically sin(x)), and no candidate formula provides this structure. The closest structures are `v*sin(t-dependent)`, `v*x`, `v/x^5`, `v*x^c`, or `v*|v|`, none of which can represent `v*sin(x)`.

After carefully reviewing all 50 candidates, none can produce the term `v*sin(x)` that appears in the ground truth.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT Equivalence Verification (PO21)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v = 0.767518*sin(t) - 0.263896*v*sin(x)**

Key observations about GT:
- It has a `sin(t)` term
- It has a `v*sin(x)` term
- No other terms (no `t`, `x`, `v` alone, no exponentials, no `|v|`, etc.)

Let me analyze each candidate by checking if unwanted terms can be zeroed out and if the required basis functions `sin(t)` and `v*sin(x)` are present.

**Important:** `cos(c + t)` with free `c` can become `sin(t)` by setting `c = -π/2`. Similarly, `v*sin(c*t + c')` with `c=0` becomes `v*sin(c')`, which is a constant times `v`, NOT `v*sin(x)`. And `v*cos(c*t + c')` with `c=0` becomes a constant times `v`.

The GT requires `v*sin(x)`. Let me check which candidates have this basis function available.

Looking through all candidates, I need to find `v*sin(x)` somewhere. Let me check terms involving both `v` and `x`:

- `v*x*cos(c*t + c')`: Setting time-dependent part to constant gives `v*x*cos(c')` = constant × `v*x`. This is `v*x`, not `v*sin(x)`.
- `v*sin(c*t + c')`: No `x` dependence.
- `v*x`: Linear in x, not `sin(x)`.
- `v/x^5`: Not `v*sin(x)`.
- `v*x^c`: Power of x, not `sin(x)`.
- `v*cos(c*t + c')`: No x dependence.
- `sin(c*x + c')`: Has sin(x) but no v multiplier.
- `v*sin(c*x + c')` in Candidate 32: `sin(c6 + c7*x + c8*v)` - this has v inside sin, not as a multiplier.

**None of the candidates contain the term `v*sin(x)`.**

Let me double-check every candidate for any possible way to produce `v*sin(x)`:

- Candidates with `v*x*cos(c*t+c')`: gives `v*x*const`, not `v*sin(x)`
- Candidates with `v*sin(c*t+c')`: gives `v*const` when c=0, not `v*sin(x)`
- Candidate 32: `sin(c6 + c7*x + c8*v)` - nonlinear in v, can't produce `v*sin(x)`
- Candidate 47: `v*x` term and `exp(c7*v)` - none give `v*sin(x)`
- Candidate 44: `x*cos(c*t+c')` - no v multiplier on sin(x)

Since `v*sin(x)` is a specific basis function (product of `v` with `sin(x)`), and none of the candidates contain any mechanism to produce this term, **no candidate can match the GT**.

The basis function `v*sin(x)` requires both: (1) `v` as a multiplicative factor, and (2) `sin(x)` as the other factor. No candidate has this combination available.
